This form must be received and signed by the Oneonta police chief by noon of the day following purchase of any antique, used or scrap jewelry. 
Penalties for violation are: 
 Every person, firm or corporation, its agents or employees, who violate any provision of the article shall be guilty of a misdemeanor and shall be punished as provided in section 1-8 of the City Code. 
(Ord. No. G-6, § 6, 12-9-80) 
Sec. 20-27. - Penalty. 
    Every person, firm or corporation, its agents or employees, who violates any provision of this article shall be guilty of a misdemeanor and shall be punished as provided in section 1-8. 
(Ord. No. G-7, § 7, 12-9-80) 
Chapter 21 - STREETS, SIDEWALKS, AND PUBLIC PLACES[1] 
Footnotes: 
--- (1) --- 
Cross reference- Casting damaging objects into streets, § 16-31; solid waste not to be deposited on streets, sidewalks, etc., § 24-37. 

ARTICLE I. - IN GENERAL 

Sec. 21-1. - Standards for accommodating utilities. 
    The city council hereby formally adopts the state highway department standards for accommodating utilities on highway rights-of-way as standards, as written, and future amendments, thereto, for use by the city for accommodating utilities on roads and streets under the jurisdiction of the city on those which have or will involve the expenditure of state or federal highway funds. 
(Ord. No. U-1, § 1, 1-11-72) 
Sec. 21-2. - Obstructing streets. 
    It shall be unlawful for any person, firm or corporation within the corporate limits or within the police jurisdiction of the city to encroach upon any streets, avenues, alleys or sidewalks or highways of the city with obstructions, or for any person, firm or corporation to allow any obstruction of any character to remain on any streets, alley, sidewalk or highway of the city, when placed there by them, and after having been notified by the police to remove same. Should a person do so, he shall be deemed guilty of a misdemeanor and upon conviction thereof shall be punished as prescribed in section 1-8. 
(Ord. No. A-55, 8-4-89) 
Secs. 21-3-21-20. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE II. - EXCAVATIONS[2] 

Footnotes: 
--- (2) --- 
Cross reference- Adoption of Standard Excavation and Grading Code, § 4-31; drainage and flood prevention, Ch. 6. 

Sec. 21-21. - Permit-Required. 
    No person, firm or corporation within the corporate limits shall dig or cause to be dug any ditch or trench in, along, or across any street, avenue, highways, or alley within the corporate limits without first securing a permit as hereinafter provided. 
(Ord. No. M-12, § 1, 1-3-58) 
Sec. 21-22. - Same-Application. 
    The city clerk, upon application made by any person, firm, or corporation for a permit to dig a ditch or trench in, along, or across any street, avenue, highway, or alley in the corporate limits will issue such permit upon the following terms and conditions: 
(1)  All work shall be subject to inspection by and approval of the street superintendent of the city. 
(2)  The installation made in the ditch or trench shall be made in such way as to interfere in no way with maintenance or with drainage along or across any street, avenue, highway, or alley. Should future maintenance, construction, or reconstruction make it necessary, this installation shall be adjusted to fit such operation at no cost to the city. 
(3)  Every precaution shall be taken to safeguard and direct the traveling public. Barricades, lights, signs, flagmen, either or all, shall be used where necessary or as directed by the superintendent. No dirt or other obstruction shall be placed on the pavement where a traffic way is provided. 
(4)  The trench shall be cut to neat lines, and caving or sloughing shall be prevented by the use of sheeting where necessary. The shoulders and ditches shall be restored to proper condition, and surplus material and rubbish shall be removed from the site. 
(5)  It is understood that the city cannot furnish full-time inspection of this work, and any feature not properly performed shall be corrected immediately upon instructions from the superintendent. 
(6)  A deposit of a certified check or bond will be required to insure the proper execution of the provision of this permit and shall be of such amount as to permit the city to perform any work not taken care of by the applicant. Check or bond to be released by the city after the applicant has met obligation as agreed and after a satisfactory maintenance period has elapsed and it is determined by the city that no further work is required. 
(7)  The method and materials to be used in the replacement of pavement shall be a minimum of ten (10) inches of concrete and approximately one and one-half (11/2) inches of bituminous materials or plant mix seal. 
(Ord. No. M-12, § 2, 1-3-58) 
Sec. 21-23. - Not applicable to city work. 
    Nothing in this article shall be construed to apply to any department or instrumentality of the city acting in the due course of its duties. 
(Ord. No. M-12, § 3, 1-3-58) 
Sec. 21-24. - Penalty. 
    Any person, firm, or corporation violating the provisions of this article shall be guilty of a misdemeanor and upon conviction; shall be punished as prescribed in section 1-8. 
(Ord. No. M-12, § 4, 1-3-58) 
Secs. 21-25-21-30. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE III. - PARADES[3] 

Footnotes: 
--- (3) --- 
Cross reference- Traffic, Ch. 23. 

Sec. 21-31. - Definitions. 
    As used in this article, the following terms are defined as follows: 
    Parade is any parade, march, ceremony, show, exhibition, pageant, or procession of any kind, or any similar display in or upon any street, park or other public place in the city. 
    Parade permit is a permit as required by this article. 
(Ord. No. P-1, § 1, 2-13-79) 
Sec. 21-32. - Permit required; exceptions. 
    It shall be unlawful for any person to engage in, participate in, aid, form or start any parade, unless a parade permit shall have been obtained from the chief of police, with the following exceptions: 
(1)  Funeral processions; 
(2)  Students going to and from school classes or participating in educational activities, providing such conduct is under the immediate direction and supervision of the proper school authorities; 
(3)  A governmental agency acting within the scope of its functions. 
(Ord. No. P-1, § 2, 2-13-79) 
Sec. 21-33. - Permit application; form. 
    A person seeking issuance of a parade permit shall file an application with the chief of police on forms provided by the chief of police. 
(Ord. No. P-1, § 3, 2-13-79) 
Sec. 21-34. - Time for filing application. 
(a)  An application for a parade permit shall be filed not less than seven (7) days nor more than twenty-one (21) days before the date on which it is proposed to conduct the parade. 
(b)  The chief of police, where good cause is shown therefor, shall have the authority to consider any application hereunder which is filed less than seven (7) days before the date such parade is proposed to be conducted. 
(Ord. No. P-1, § 5, 2-13-79) 
Sec. 21-35. - Contents of permit application. 
    The application for a parade permit shall set forth the following information: 
(1)  The name, address and telephone number of the person seeking to conduct such parade; 
(2)  If the parade is proposed to be conducted for, on behalf of, or by an organization, the name, address and telephone number of the headquarters of the organization, and of the authorized and responsible heads of such organization; 
(3)  The name, address and telephone number of the person who will be the parade chairman and who will be responsible for its conduct; 
(4)  The date when the parade is to be conducted; 
(5)  The route to be traveled, the starting point and the termination point; 
(6)  The approximate number of persons who, and animals and vehicles which, will constitute such parade; the type of animals, and description of the vehicles; 
(7)  The time when such parade will start and terminate; 
(8)  A statement as to whether the parade will occupy all or any portion the width of the streets proposed to be traversed; 
(9)  The location by streets of any assembly areas for such parade; 
(10)  The time at which units of the parade will begin to assemble at any such assembly areas; 
(11)  The interval of space to be maintained between units of such parade; 
(12)  If the parade is designed to be held by, and on behalf of or for, any person other than the applicant, the applicant for such permit shall file with the chief of police a communication in writing from the person proposing to hold the parade authorizing the applicant to apply for the permit on his behalf; 
(13)  Any additional information which the chief of police shall find reasonably necessary to a fair determination as to whether a permit should issue. 
(Ord. No. P-1, § 4, 2-13-79) 
Sec. 21-36. - Permit fee. 
    There shall be paid at the time of filing the application for a parade permit a fee of five dollars ($5.00). 
(Ord. No. P-1, § 6, 2-13-79) 
Sec. 21-37. - Contents of permit. 
    Each parade permit shall state the following information: 
(1)  Starting time; 
(2)  Minimum speed; 
(3)  Maximum speed; 
(4)  Maximum interval of space to be maintained between the units of the parade; 
(5)  The portions of the streets to be traversed that may be occupied by the parade; 
(6)  The maximum length of the parade in miles or fractions thereof; 
(7)  Such other information as the chief of police shall fine necessary to the enforcement of this article. 
(Ord. No. P-1, § 11, 2-13-79) 
Sec. 21-38. - Standards of issuance. 
    The chief of police shall issue a permit as provided for in this article when, from a consideration of the application and from such other information as may otherwise be obtained, he finds that: 
(1)  The conduct of the parade will not substantially interrupt the safe and orderly movement of other traffic contiguous to its route; 
(2)  The conduct of the parade will not require the diversion of so great a number of police officers of the city properly to police the line of movement and the areas contiguous thereto as to prevent normal police protection to the city; 
(3)  The conduct of such parade will not require the diversion of so great a number of ambulances as to prevent normal ambulance service to portions of the city other than to be occupied by the proposed line of march and areas contiguous thereto; 
(4)  The concentration of persons, animals and vehicles at assembly points of the parade will not unduly interfere with proper fire and police protection of, or ambulance service to, areas contiguous to such assembly areas; 
(5)  The conduct of such parade will not interfere with the movement of firefighting equipment en route to a fire; 
(6)  The conduct of the parade is not reasonably likely to cause injury to persons or property, to provoke disorderly conduct or create a disturbance; 
(7)  The parade is scheduled to move from its point of origin to its point of termination expeditiously and without unreasonable delays en route; 
(8)  The parade is not to be held for the sole purpose of advertising any product, goods or event, and is not designed to be held purely for private profit. 
(Ord. No. P-1, § 7, 2-13-79) 
Sec. 21-39. - Acting on application; notice of rejection. 
    The chief of police shall act upon the application for a parade permit within two (2) days after the filing thereof. If the chief of police disapproves the application, he shall mail to the applicant within three (3) days after the date upon which the application was filed, a notice of his action, stating the reasons for his denial of the permit. 
(Ord. No. P-1, § 8, 2-13-79) 
Sec. 21-40. - Alternative date, time or route. 
    The chief of police, in denying an application for a parade permit, shall be empowered to authorize the conduct of the parade on a date, at a time, or over a route different from that named by the applicant. An applicant desiring to accept an alternate permit shall, within two (2) days after notice of the action of the chief of police, file a written notice of acceptance with the chief of police. An alternate parade permit shall conform to the requirements of and shall have the effect of a parade permit under this article. 
(Ord. No. P-1, § 10, 2-13-79) 
Sec. 21-41. - Appeal to council. 
    Any person aggrieved by the denial of a parade permit shall have the right to appeal the denial to the council. The appeal shall be taken within two (2) days after notice that the application has been denied. The council shall act upon the appeal within two (2) days after its receipt. 
(Ord. No. P-1, § 9, 2-13-79) 
Sec. 21-42. - Notice to city officials. 
    Immediately upon the issuance of a parade permit, the chief of police shall send a copy thereof to the following: 
(1)  The mayor. 
(2)  The city attorney. 
(Ord. No. P-1, § 12, 2-13-79) 
Sec. 21-43. - Compliance with laws; chairman to carry permit. 
(a)  The holder of a parade permit hereunder shall comply with all permit directions and conditions and with all applicable laws, provisions of this Code and other city ordinances. 
(b)  The parade chairman or other person heading or leading such activity shall carry the parade permit upon his person during the conduct of the parade. 
(Ord. No. P-1, § 13, 2-13-79) 
Sec. 21-44. - Revocation of permit. 
    The chief of police shall have the authority to revoke a parade permit issued hereunder upon application of the standards for issuance as established in this article. 
(Ord. No. P-1, § 14, 2-13-79) 
Sec. 21-45. - Public conduct during parade. 
(a)  Interference. It shall be unlawful for any person to unreasonably hamper, obstruct or impede, or interfere with any parade or parade assembly or with any person, vehicle or animal participating or used in a parade. 
(b)  Driving through parades. It shall be unlawful for any person to drive a vehicle between the vehicles or persons comprising a parade when such vehicles or persons are in motion and are conspicuously designated as a parade. 
(c)  Parking on parade route. The chief of police shall have the authority, when reasonably necessary, to prohibit or restrict the parking of vehicles along a highway or part thereof constituting a part of the route of a parade. The chief of police shall post signs to such effect, and it shall be unlawful for any person to park or leave unattended any vehicle in violation thereof. No person shall be liable for parking on a street unposted in violation of this section. 
(Ord. No. P-1, § 15, 2-13-79) 
Chapter 22 - SUBDIVISIONS[1] 

Footnotes:

    Nothing in this Code or the ordinance adopting this Code effects the city's subdivision regulations, adopted in Ord. No. Z-2, on December 29, 1964, as amended. Such regulations are recognized as continuing in full force and effect to the same extent as if set out at length in this Code. 
Sec. 22-2. - Street specifications. 
    The "Minimum Specifications for Construction of Streets, City of Oneonta, Alabama," as approved November 30, 1964, and prepared by Mabry Engineering Company, Decatur, Alabama, are hereby adopted. 
(Ord. No. Z-2, § 1, 12-29-64)
