Chapter 23 - TRAFFIC AND VEHICLES[1] 
Footnotes: 
--- (1) --- 
Cross reference- Municipal court magistrate's responsibility for uniform traffic tickets, § 5-5; obstructing streets, § 21-2; parades, § 21-31 et seq. 

ARTICLE I. - IN GENERAL 

Sec. 23-1. - State laws adopted. 
(a)  In addition to all other provisions of law relating the speed and operation of motor vehicles in the city, there is hereby adopted by the city all laws of the state and all rules and regulations of the state highway department pertaining to the control of traffic and motor vehicles on highways, that are misdemeanors under the state laws and a violation of such laws, rules and regulations in the city in the police jurisdiction thereof, shall be a violation of this chapter. 
(b)  Any person violating any provisions of this section shall be guilty of a misdemeanor and shall, upon conviction thereof, be punished by a fine of not more than two hundred dollars ($200.00) or may be imprisoned in the municipal jail or sentenced to hard labor for the city, for a period not exceeding ten (10) days. For a second conviction within one (1) year thereafter, such person shall be punished by a fine of not more than two hundred dollars ($200.00) or may be imprisoned in the municipal jail or sentenced to hard labor for the city for a period not exceeding twenty (20) days or both such fine and imprisonment. Upon a third or subsequent conviction within one (1) year after the first conviction, such person shall be punished by a fine of not more than two hundred dollars ($200.00) or may be imprisoned in the municipal jail or sentenced to hard labor for the city for a period not exceeding six (6) months or both fine and imprisonment. 
Editor's note- Sections 3 and 5 of an ordinance adopted June 26, 1990, providing for the adoption of state regulations controlling traffic and motor vehicles, and providing penalties for violations, has been treated as being amendatory of § 23-1. 
(Ord. No. S-6, § 8, 11-14-72; Ord. of 6-26-90, §§ 3, 5) 
Cross reference- State offenses adopted, § 16-1. 
Sec. 23-2. - Train speed limit. 
    Speed for trains within the corporate limits of the city is hereby set at twenty-five (25) miles per hour. 
(Ord. No. T-47, § 1, 11-10-81) 
Sec. 23-3. - Photoelectric intoximeter test. 
    The city in compliance with section 1(a) of Act No. 699 adopted at the 1969 regular session of the Legislature of Alabama does hereby designate the chemical analysis of the breath by use of the photoelectric intoximeter as the test to be administered by its officers approved by the state department of health pursuant to section 2(b) of Act No. 699 adopted at the 1969 regular session of the Legislature of Alabama, to determine the alcoholic content of the blood of any person lawfully arrested for any offense arising out of acts alleged to have been committed while the person was driving a motor vehicle on the public highways of the state while under the influence of intoxicating liquor. 
(Ord. No. I-1, § 1, 1-14-75) 
Sec. 23-4. - Sale of motor vehicles on private property. 
    Except for the owner of a private motor vehicle offering his own vehicle for sale on his own private property, no person shall offer for sale a motor vehicle of any kind, whether attended or not, upon any private property within the city not properly zoned and licensed for the sale of motor vehicles. Any person violating any of the provisions hereof shall be punished under the provisions of section 1-8 of this Code. 
    Additionally, the police department of the city is hereby authorized to cause any motor vehicle for sale in violation of this section to be removed and stored at an authorized location and the costs of such removal and storage shall be at the expense of the owner of such motor vehicle. 
(Ord. No. 23-12-6, 11-28-95) 
Editor's note- Ordinance No. 23-12-6, adopted November 28, 1995, did not specifically amend the Code; hence, codification of substantive provisions as § 23-4 was at the discretion of the editor. 
Sec. 23-5. - Impoundment of vehicles driven by unlicensed persons. 
(a)  Definitions. For the purposes of this section, the following words shall have the following meanings: 
    Impounding agency means the City of Oneonta Police Department. 
    Legal owner means a lienholder, person with a security interest in a motor vehicle, a lessor of a motor vehicle, assignee of the lessor, or the person who is the registered owner of the motor vehicle. 
(b)  Conditions; exceptions. 
(1)  Notwithstanding any other provisions of law, and except as otherwise provided in this section, a motor vehicle is subject to impoundment as a nuisance if it is driven on a highway or other public roadway in the city and any of the following conditions exist: The motor vehicle is driven by a person whose license or license privilege is suspended or revoked at the time he or she was stopped for having been previously convicted of driving under the influence of alcohol or controlled substance, including, but not limited to, being adjudicated delinquent or a youthful offender based on a DUI-related offense, as defined in Section 32-5A-191 of the Code of Alabama 1975. 
(2)  [Exceptions.] 
a.  If a driver is unable to produce a valid driver's license on the demand of the law enforcement officer, the vehicle shall be impounded regardless of ownership, unless the police officer is reasonably able, by other means, to verify that the driver is properly licensed. Prior to impounding the vehicle, a law enforcement officer shall make a reasonable attempt to verify the license status of a driver who claims to be properly licensed, but who is unable to produce the license on demand of the law enforcement officer. A notation of the officer's attempt to verify that the driver is properly licensed shall be noted on the arrest report. The driver and occupants of the vehicle will be transported to a place of safety by the impounding officer and a pull in report made with a full inventory of items in the vehicle. 
b.  A law enforcement officer shall not impound a vehicle pursuant to this section if the license of the driver expired within the preceding ninety (90) days and the driver would otherwise have been properly licensed. 
c.  If the owner of the vehicle or another family member of the owner is present in the vehicle and has a valid license, the vehicle shall not be impounded and towed. 
d.  If there is a medical necessity jeopardizing life or limb, the law enforcement officer may elect not to impound the vehicle. 
(c)  Administration. 
(1)  [Proof of license.] The registered owner or his/her representative appears at the city police department or a representative with written notarized authorization from the registered owner appears, and presents a valid driver's license, a copy of the title, tag receipt, or notarized bill of sale, and a copy of the written authorization, if applicable, to be copied by the police department. 
(2)  If the registered owner does not have a valid driver's license he/she may bring someone with them who has a verified valid license and the vehicle may be released without written notarized permission. 
(3)  Any owner of a vehicle who suffers any loss due to the impoundment of any vehicle pursuant to this section may recover the amount of the loss from the unlicensed, suspended, or revoked driver. 
(d)  Fees. The person redeeming the vehicle at the wrecker lot will be responsible for paying the set towing and storage fee as well as an administrative fee to be forwarded by the wrecker company to the city in the amount of ten dollars ($10.00) per vehicle. This fee will help the city defer the administrative cost for enforcement of the section, and can change from time to time as administrative costs increase. 
(e)  Unredeemed vehicles. Any vehicle impounded that is not redeemed pursuant to this section within sixty (60) days may be sold by the wrecker company for fees owed according to state law. 
(Ord. No. M-38-98-1, §§ 2-6, 6-23-98) 
Editor's note- Ordinance No. M-38-98-1, adopted June 23, 1998, did not specifically amend the Code; hence, codification of §§ 2-6 of said ordinance as § 23-5 was at the discretion of the editor. 
Secs. 23-6-23-30. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE II. - OPERATION 

Sec. 23-31. - Truck routes. 
(a)  There is hereby established a truck route for northbound motor trucks (except trucks known as pickup trucks), road tractors, semitrailers and pole trailers on U.S. Highway 231, to be known as "truck route U.S. 231 North." The truck route is more particularly described as follows: 
(1)  For vehicles traveling north on U.S. Highway 231 from the southeast begin at the intersection of U.S. Highway 231 and First Avenue; thence turn to the left on First Avenue to the intersection of Fifth Street; thence right on Fifth Street in a northwest direction to intersect Alabama Highway 75, and continuing north along Fifth Street, also designated as U.S. 231, and point of ending of the truck route. 
(2)  For vehicles traveling southwesterly on Alabama Highway 75 wishing to go on U.S. 231 North; beginning at the intersection of Alabama Highway 75 and Fifth Street, also known as U.S. Highway 231, thence turn right and proceed northwesterly along Fifth Street or U.S. Highway 231, and point of ending. 
(3)  For vehicles traveling northeast on Alabama Highway 75 turning on U.S. Highway 231 north, beginning at the intersection of Alabama Highway 75 with Second Street; thence turn left on Second Street and in a northwest direction along Second Street to the intersection of Second Street with State Road; thence turning to the right and in a northeast direction along State Road to where State Road intersects U.S. Highway 231 and point of ending of the truck route. 
(b)  All northbound motor trucks (except trucks known as pickup trucks), road tractors, semitrailers, and pole trailers on U.S. Highway 231 shall travel on the designated truck route known as "truck route U.S. 231 north." 
(c)  The police department of the city in cooperation with the highway department of the state is hereby authorized to place and maintain traffic control devices to indicate and carry out the provisions of this section. 
(d)  It shall be unlawful and a violation of this section for any person to operate a motor truck (except trucks known as pickup trucks), road tractor, semitrailer, or pole trailer northbound on U.S. Highway 231, upon any street, avenue, or highway in the city except on truck route U.S. Highway 231 North as herein designated. 
(e)  Any person who operates a motor truck (except trucks known as pickup trucks), road tractor, semitrailer or police trailer north bound on U.S. Highway 231 in violation of this section shall be deemed guilty of a misdemeanor and upon conviction, shall be punished as prescribed in section 1-8. 
(Ord. No. T-44, §§ 1-5, 3-13-79) 
Sec. 23-32. - Speed limits. 
(a)  No person shall operate a motor vehicle at a greater speed than fifty-five (55) miles per hour, in the following listed zones of the city: 
(1)  On Alabama Highway 132, from the east city limits, westward a distance of 0.45 miles. 
(2)  On Alabama Highway 53 (U.S. 231) from the south city limits, northward a distance of 0.32 miles. 
(3)  On Alabama Highway 53 (U.S. 231), from the north city limits, southward a distance of 1.49 miles. 
(b)  No person shall operate a motor vehicle at a greater speed than fifty (50) miles per hour in the following listed zones of the city: 
(1)  On Alabama Highway 53 (U.S. 231), beginning 0.32 miles north of the south city limits, northward a distance of 1.05 miles. 
(2)  On Alabama Highway 75, beginning at the north city limits southward a distance of 2.10 miles. 
(3)  On Alabama Highway 132, beginning 0.45 miles west of the east city limits, westward a distance of 0.70 miles. 
(4)  Along Alabama 53 (U.S. 231), within the city limits, from mile post 253.0 to mile post 253.55. (Ord. of 6-26-90, § 1) 
(c)  No person shall operate a motor vehicle at a greater speed than forty-five (45) miles per hour in the following listed zones in the city: 
(1)  On Alabama Highway 53 (U.S. 231), beginning 1.49 miles south of the north city limits southward a distance of 0.47 miles. 
(2)  On Alabama Highway 132, from the east city limits, westward a distance of 0.45 miles. 
(3)  On Highway 75 north from the north city limits southward 0.70 of a mile to mile post 31. (Ord. of 12-12-89, § 1) 
(4)  On Alabama Highway 53 (also known as U.S. Highway 231), beginning at mile post 253.15 and continuing northward a distance of 0.55 miles. (Ord. of 12-12-89, § 3) 
(5)  Along Alabama 53 (U.S. 231), within the city limits, from mile post 253.55 to mile post 254.30. (Ord. of 6-26-90, § 1) 
(6)  Along Alabama 53 (U.S. 231), within the city limits, from mile post 255.35 to mile post 255.65. (Ord. of 6-26-90, § 1) 
(7)  Along Alabama 75, within the city limits, from mile post 27.25 to mile post 28.35. (Ord. of 6-26-90, § 1) 
(8)  Along Alabama 75, within the city limits, from mile post 30.15 to mile post 31.70. (Ord. of 6-26-90, § 1) 
(d)  No person shall operate a motor vehicle at a greater speed than thirty-five (35) miles per hour in the following listed zones of the city: 
(1)  On Alabama Highway 53 (U.S. 231), beginning 1.37 miles north of the south city limits, northward a distance of 0.91 miles. 
(2)  On Alabama Highway 75, beginning 1.05 miles north of the south city limits, northward a distance of 1.45 miles. 
(3)  On Alabama Highway 132, beginning 1.15 miles west of the east city limits, westward a distance of 0.42 miles. 
(4)  On Second Street North, beginning at the intersection of Second Street North and Second Avenue East, to the intersection of Second Street and State Road. 
(5)  On State Road, from intersection of State Road and Second Street North, to intersection of State Road and Alabama Highway 53 (U.S. 231). 
(6)  On Highway 75 North at a point 1.05 miles north of the south city limits for a distance of 2.06 miles to mile post 31. (Ord. of 12-12-89, § 2) 
(7)  On Alabama Highway 53 (also known as U.S. Highway 231), beginning at mile post 253.70 proceeding northward a distance of 1.51 miles. (Ord. of 12-12-89, § 4) 
(8)  Along Alabama 53 (U.S. 231), within the city limits, from mile post 254.30 to mile post 255.35. (Ord. of 6-26-90, § 1) 
(9)  Along Alabama 75, within the city limits, from mile post 28.35 to mile post 30.15. (Ord. of 6-26-90, § 1) 
(e)  No person shall operate a motor vehicle at a greater speed than twenty-five (25) miles per hour on any streets or alleys not specifically mentioned or set out herein. 
(f)  Speed limits as described above shall apply so long as the city limits remain as they are this date. In the event they are extended, this section shall be revised to properly cover the new territory. 
(g)  Any person violating any provisions of this section shall be guilty of a misdemeanor and shall, upon conviction thereof, be punished by a fine of not more than two hundred dollars ($200.00) or may be imprisoned in the municipal jail or sentenced to hard labor for the city, for a period not exceeding ten (10) days. For a second conviction within one (1) year thereafter, such person shall be punished by a fine of not more than two hundred dollars ($200.00) or may be imprisoned in the municipal jail or sentenced to hard labor for the city for a period not exceeding twenty (20) days or both such fine and imprisonment. Upon a third or subsequent conviction within one (1) year after the first conviction, such person shall be punished by a fine of not more than two hundred dollars ($200.00) or may be imprisoned in the municipal jail or sentenced to hard labor for the city for a period not exceeding six (6) months or both fine and imprisonment. (Ord. of 6-26-90, § 5) 
(Ord. No. S-6, §§ 1-6, 11-14-72) 
Editor's note- Ordinances adopted Dec. 12, 1989 and June 26, 1990, have been treated as amendatory of § 23-32; however, inasmuch as such ordinances did not specify manner of inclusion, it is presumed that in the event of conflicting speed limits, the more recent provisions will prevail. 
Sec. 23-33. - Turns generally; U-turns. 
    No person shall turn any vehicle around in any of the streets, avenues, alleys or highway, except at the intersection of streets, avenues, alleys or highways. There shall be no U-turns at the intersection of First Avenue and Second Street, nor at the intersection of First Avenue and Third Street. 
(Ord. No. A-39, 8-9-37) 
Sec. 23-34. - Driving through property to avoid traffic signal. 
(a)  It shall be unlawful for any person operating any motor vehicle within the city or its police jurisdiction to drive such vehicle through private or public property for the purpose of avoiding a traffic light or traffic signal at such property. 
(b)  Driving a motor vehicle through any private or public property located at the intersection of any two (2) streets of the city without stopping such vehicle on such property for the transaction of business shall be prima facie evidence of a violation of this section. 
(c)  The minimum fine established for a violation of this section is twenty dollars ($20.00). The maximum fine shall be governed by the general ordinance for violations of the Municipal Code, as otherwise set forth in section 1-8. 
(Ord. No. M-38-97-1, 4-8-97) 
Secs. 23-35-23-50. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE III. - STOPPING, STANDING AND PARKING[2] 

Footnotes: 
--- (2) --- 
Cross reference- Parking or parade route, § 21-45. 

Sec. 23-51. - Manner of parking-Generally. 
    It shall be unlawful to park an automobile or truck except on the right-hand side of the street and within the lines where parking spaces are marked off. Trucks shall only be allowed to park in parking spaces for the purpose of loading and unloading and shall be allowed two (2) spaces for that purpose in order to clear the outside parking lines. 
(Ord. No. A-6, 5-7-35) 
Sec. 23-52. - Same-On state highways or unpaved ways. 
    It shall be unlawful for any person to park any vehicle on the paved part of any state highway within the corporate limits of the city or within its police jurisdiction, or to park any vehicle on the traveled part of any highway, which is unpaved; or to in any way block or partially block any highway by the parking of any vehicle. 
(Ord. No. A-47, 8-1-38) 
Sec. 23-53. - Parking limits to twelve hours in one place. 
    It shall be unlawful for any person, firm or corporation to park, place or leave any vehicle, motor driven, motor pulled, or with other means of location, on any of the streets, avenues, roads, passways, or alleys within the corporate limits for a longer space of time than twelve (12) hours. At the conclusion of twelve (12) hours of standing in one (1) place, the chief of police or other police officer, or person authorized to do so, shall notify the owner or owners of the vehicle of its position; and if same be an obstruction to traffic, or otherwise a nuisance to the public welfare, the same shall from and after the time of said notice become a misdemeanor. Each hour the vehicle shall remain in the same location, after due notice, shall constitute a separate offense and may be so prosecuted. Should it be impossible to locate the owner or owners thereof, then the chief of police, or other police officer, or other persons authorized shall take the vehicle in charge, store same, and shall collect all costs of such taking charge and storage before returning the vehicle to the proper owner. 
(Ord. No. A-23, 1-20-36) 
Sec. 23-54. - Two-hour parking zones. 
(a)  The following limited motor vehicle parking zones are established: 
First Avenue, each side, from First Street to Fourth Street 
Second Avenue, each side, from Second Street to Fourth Street 
Second Street, each side, from Third Avenue to Railroad Alley 
Third Avenue, each side, from Second Street to Fourth Street, and designated and marked areas on Railroad Avenue 
Third Street, each side, from Third Avenue to Railroad Alley 
Fourth Street, each side, from Second Avenue to Railroad Alley 
(b)  No person shall park, cause to be parked, or knowingly permit an automobile or other motor vehicle which he owns, to be parked in any parking zone within the city for a period of time in excess of two (2) hours between the hours of 8:00 a.m. and 5:00 p.m. on each day of the week except Sundays and legal holidays. 
(c)  The chief of police is authorized and is hereby directed to mar or cause to be marked the parking zones, and spaces therein, in accordance with this section and to post signs designating the time limit for occupancy of such parking zones. 
(d)  No person shall park, cause to be parked, or knowingly permit an automobile or other motor vehicle which he owns to be parked, on any street in the city in violation of this section. The penalty for parking contrary and in violation of this section shall be a fine of five dollars ($5.00) provided that payment for such parking violation is made within forty-eight (48) hours from the issuance of the citation for the violation. If such parking violation fine is not paid within the forty-eight-hour period subsequent to the issuance of the citation for the parking violation, the fine shall be ten dollars ($10.00) each and every violation shall constitute a separate offense. 
(Ord. No. T-45, §§ 1-4, 5-8-79; Ord. of 1-15-86) 
Sec. 23-55. - Parking in no parking areas. 
    No person shall park a motor vehicle in any designated area when the prohibited area is properly marked with yellow paint or signed. The penalty for parking contrary and in violation of this section shall be a fine of five dollars ($5.00) provided that payment for such parking violation is made within forty-eight (48) hours from the issuance of the citation for the violation. If such parking violation fine is not paid within the forty-eight-hour period subsequent to the issuance of the citation for the parking violation, the fine shall be ten dollars ($10.00) each and every violation shall constitute a separate offense. 
(Ord. No. S-6, § 7, 11-14-72; Ord. of 6-26-90, § 4; Ord. of 1-22-91) 
Sec. 23-56. - Parking on wrong side of road. 
    No person shall park a motor vehicle in any designated parking space where the motor vehicle shall be parked on the opposite side of the road for the direction in which such motor vehicle is traveling. (By way of example, no motor vehicle shall be parked in a parking space such that the motor vehicle is heading north when the parking space is adjacent to a southbound lane). The penalty for parking contrary and in violation of this section shall be a fine of ten dollars ($10.00) provided that payment for such parking violation is made within forty-eight (48) hours from the issuance of the citation for the violation. If such parking violation fine is not paid within the forty-eight-hour period subsequent to the issuance of the citation for the parking violation, the fine shall be twenty dollars ($20.00) each and every violation shall constitute a separate offense. 
(Ord. of 1-22-91) 
Sec. 23-57. - Parking in handicapped space. 
    No person shall park a motor vehicle in any designated handicapped parking space, area or zone. The penalty for parking contrary and in violation of this section shall be a fine of twenty-five dollars ($25.00) provided that payment for such parking violation is made within forty-eight (48) hours from the issuance of the citation for the violation. If such parking violation fine is not paid within the forty-eight-hour period subsequent to the issuance of the citation for the parking violation, the fine shall be fifty dollars ($50.00) each and every violation shall constitute a separate offense. 
(Ord. of 1-22-91) 
Sec. 23-58. - Blocking fire lane or fire plug. 
    No person shall park a motor vehicle so as to block a fire lane or any fire plug. The penalty for parking contrary and in violation of this section shall be a fine of twenty-five dollars ($25.00) provided that payment for such parking violation is made within forty-eight (48) hours from the issuance of the citation for the violation. If such parking violation fine is not paid within the forty-eight-hour period subsequent to the issuance of the citation for the parking violation, the fine shall be fifty dollars ($50.00) each and every violation shall constitute a separate offense. 
(Ord. of 1-22-91) 
Sec. 23-59. - Blocking alleyway or roadway. 
    No person shall park a motor vehicle so as to block any public alleyway or roadway. The penalty for parking contrary and in violation of this section shall be a fine of ten dollars ($10.00) provided that payment for such parking violation is made within forty-eight (48) hours from the issuance of the citation for the violation. If such parking violation fine is not paid within the forty-eight-hour period subsequent to the issuance of the citation for the parking violation, the fine shall be twenty dollars ($20.00) each and every violation shall constitute a separate offense. 
(Ord. of 1-22-91) 
Secs. 23-60-23-80. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE IV. - BICYCLES 
DIVISION 1. - GENERALLY 

Sec. 23-81. - Bicycle lights. 
    It shall be unlawful for any person to ride or drive a tricycle or bicycle within the city limits or the police jurisdiction thereof, without having one (1) headlight and one (1) taillight or reflector, in good condition and burning between the hours of dusk and dawn. 
(Ord. No. A-57, 10-3-39) 
Secs. 23-82-23-88. - Reserved. 
DIVISION 2. - BICYCLE SAFETY[3] 

Footnotes: 
--- (3) --- 
Editor's note- Ord. No. C-1, §§ 1-6, adopted July 12, 1994, did not specify manner of codification; hence, codification of the substantive provisions as Div. 3, §§ 23-89-23-94 was at the discretion of the editor. 

Sec. 23-89. - Definitions. 
    The following definitions are adopted for this title: 
    Bicycle shall mean a vehicle with two (2) wheels, propelled solely by human power and having pedals and handle bars. The term "bicycle" shall include bicycles for two (2) or more persons having seats and corresponding sets of pedals arranged in tandem. The term "bicycle" specifically excludes tricycles. 
    Guardian means a parent, legal guardian, or temporary guardian who maintains responsibility, whether voluntary or otherwise, for the safety and welfare of a person under the age of sixteen (16) years. 
    Low income persons shall mean a person under the age of sixteen (16) years who qualifies for the school lunch program presently in effect, or a parent, legal guardian or temporary guardian of a person under the age of sixteen (16) years who qualifies for the school lunch program presently in effect. 
(Ord. No. C-1, § 1, 7-12-94) 
Sec. 23-90. - General requirements regarding bicycle helmets. 
(a)  Any person operating or riding on a bicycle on a public roadway, bicycle path or on any right of way or publicly owned facility under the jurisdiction of the city shall wear a properly fitted and fastened helmet designed for bicycle safety. Such helmet shall meet or exceed the requirements of the American National Standards Institute ("ANSI") (Z90.4 Bicycle Helmet Standard) or the Snell Memorial Foundation's 1984 Standard for Protective Headgear for Use in Bicycling, or such subsequent nationally recognized standard for bicycle helmet use as the city may adopt. The helmet must be equipped with either a neck or chin strap that shall be fastened securely while the bicycle is in motion. 
(b)  The guardian of a person under the age of sixteen (16) years shall not knowingly allow, or fail to take reasonable steps to prevent, their child or ward ("minor") from operating or riding a bicycle on a public roadway, bicycle path, on any right of way or publicly owned facility under the jurisdiction of the city, unless that minor is wearing a helmet that meets the requirements of section 23-90(a) above. 
(c)  No person shall transport another person upon a bicycle on a public roadway, bicycle path or any right of way of publicly owned facility under the jurisdiction of the city, unless that other person is wearing a helmet that meets the requirements of section 23-90(a) above. 
(Ord. No. C-1, § 2, 7-12-94) 
Sec. 23-91. - Enforcement. 
(a)  The Oneonta Police Department must enforce the bicycle helmet requirement of this division. Any other duly commissioned law enforcement officer having law enforcement authority at the place where a violation of this division occurs is authorized to enforce the provisions of this division. 
(b)  Any person found to have committed a violation of this division shall be assessed a monetary penalty of twenty-five dollars ($25.00) for the first such violation. Any subsequent offense of this division is punishable by a maximum fine of twenty-five dollars ($25.00) greater for each subsequent offense up to a maximum of one hundred dollars ($100.00) for an offense. (i.e., second offense fifty dollars ($50.00), third offense seventy-five dollars ($75.00) and fourth offense one hundred dollars ($100.00)). 
(c)  Notwithstanding the provisions of section 23-91(b) above, the fine for a person's first violation of this division must be waived if 
(1)  The person charged: 
(a)  Is a minor; and 
(b)  Produces proof to the Oneonta Police Department or city clerk that they have obtained a bicycle helmet for their use within ten (10) days of the violation; 
(2)  The person charged: 
(a)  Is the guardian of a minor; and 
(b)  Produces proof to the Oneonta Police Department or city clerk that they have obtained a bicycle helmet for use by the minor within ten (10) days of the violation; or 
(3)  The person charged: 
(a)  Is not a minor; and 
(b)  Produces proof to the Oneonta Police Department or city clerk that they have obtained a bicycle helmet for their use within ten (10) days of the violation. 
(d)  Notwithstanding the provisions set forth above, the court may waive, reduce or suspend the monetary penalties described herein and impose such conditions on a waiver, reduction or suspension as it deems just. If the court determines that a person has insufficient funds to pay the monetary penalty, the court may enter the performance of a number of hours of community service in lieu of a monetary penalty, at the rate of the then state minimum wage per hour. 
(e)  All moneys collected as fines under section 23-91(b) shall be deposited in a nonlapsing revolving fund to be known as the "Bicycle Safety Fund". Interest earned on money deposited in the fund shall accrue to the fund. Money in the fund shall be utilized to provide educational programs devoted to bicycle safety. If it is determined that sufficient money is available in the fund, money shall be used to assist low income persons in purchasing bicycle helmets meeting the standards set forth in section 23-90(a). For purposes of this subsection, "low income persons" shall be determined according to standards to be adopted by the city and available from the city clerk. 
(Ord. No. C-1, § 3, 7-12-94) 
Sec. 23-92. - Education requirement. 
    The city has made a determination that further educating persons regarding the benefits of wearing appropriate bicycle helmets will encourage those persons riding bicycles to use helmets. Accordingly, at the time of any citation or within five (5) days thereafter, the Oneonta Police Department of the City Clerk will provide to the offending party appropriate educational materials concerning the use of bicycle helmets. 
(Ord. No. C-1, § 4, 7-12-94) 
Sec. 23-93. - Evidence of negligence. 
    Failure of a person to use a bicycle helmet as required by this division or evidence that a guardian of a minor knowingly allowed the minor to violate the bicycle helmet requirement of this division will not be considered evidence of negligence or contributory negligence in any civil action. 
(Ord. No. C-1, § 5, 7-12-94) 
Sec. 23-94. - Transition period. 
    During the first ninety (90) days after the effective date of this division, the penalty for violating this division is limited to a warning to the offender, and if the offender be a minor, the offender's guardian, (a) about the bicycle helmet requirements of this division; and (b) providing educational materials about bicycle helmet use. 
(Ord. No. C-1, § 6, 7-12-94) 
Secs. 23-95-23-100. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE V. - EMERGENCY VEHICLES 

Sec. 23-101. - Ambulance clearance required. 
(a)  It shall be unlawful for the operator of any ambulance or oxygen service vehicle to operate an ambulance or oxygen service vehicle within the city limits or its police jurisdiction on an emergency response without first having secured a verbal clearance from the radio dispatcher of the police department of the city. 
(b)  A clearance for an emergency response within the city or its police jurisdiction shall be secured by contacting the radio dispatcher of the police department of the city by telephone or radio, giving the dispatcher information as to the nature of the emergency, the route of proposed travel, the destination and the direction of travel. The radio dispatcher shall log each such request and will disseminate such information to police department personnel and fire department personnel of the city as may be appropriate. 
(c)  Any person found to be in violation of this section shall, upon conviction, be punished as provided in section 1-8. 
(Ord. No. E-2, §§ 1-3, 10-13-87) 
Sec. 23-102. - Ambulance speed in intersections. 
    It shall be unlawful for the driver of any ambulance or oxygen service vehicle to cause or allow the same to enter or cross a street intersection at a speed in excess of ten (10) miles per hour while a red or amber traffic signal light is displayed in or against the path or direction of his travel. Any person who shall within the corporate limits or within the police jurisdiction violate any of the provisions of this section shall be guilty of misdemeanor and, upon conviction, shall be punished as prescribed in section 1-8. 
(Ord. No. M-10, 12-7-56) 
Secs. 23-103-23-120. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE VI. - ABANDONED VEHICLES 

Sec. 23-121. - Definitions. 
    For the purpose of this article, the following terms, phrases, words and their derivations shall have the meanings given herein. When not inconsistent with the context, words used in the present tense include the future, words in the plural noun include the singular noun, and words in the singular noun include the plural noun. The word "shall" is always mandatory and not merely directory. 
    City shall mean the City of Oneonto, Alabama. 
    Person shall mean any person, firm, partnership, association, corporation, company, or organization of any kind. 
    Street or highway shall mean the entire width between the boundary lines of every way publicly maintained when any part thereof is open to the use of the public for purposes of vehicular travel. 
    Vehicle shall mean a machine propelled by power other than human power designed to travel along the ground by use of wheels, treads, runners, or slides and to transport persons or property or to pull machinery and shall include, without limitation, automobile, truck, trailer, motorcycle, tractor, buggy and wagon. 
(Ord. No. V-1A, § 1, 6-6-67) 
Sec. 23-122. - What constitutes abandoned vehicle. 
    Any vehicle or portion thereof left standing or parked on any street or within the right-of-way boundaries of any street, alley, or other public way within the limits of the city will be deemed to be abandoned, lost, stolen or unclaimed if the same is allowed to remain parked or left standing on any such street or within any such right-of-way for a period of seven (7) consecutive days. 
(Ord. No. V-1A, § 2, 6-16-67) 
Sec. 23-123. - Towing and storage. 
    The chief of police or his duly authorized representative is hereby authorized and directed to tow or haul away or cause to be towed or hauled away to a central collecting point of his designation any vehicle left standing on any city street or within any such right-of-way boundary for more than seven (7) consecutive days and cause the same to be stored. The chief of police of the city shall keep a permanent record giving the date of the taking of each such vehicle, the place where found and taken, and a description of each such vehicle. 
(Ord. No. V-1A, § 3, 6-6-67) 
Sec. 23-124. - Release from storage. 
    Upon proper proof of ownership or possession satisfactory to the chief of police of the city, the owner or person entitled to possession may reclaim any such vehicle which has been towed or hauled away upon payment by such person to the city the costs of towing or hauling away plus the payment of all other reasonable charges as may be charged by the depository for storing such vehicle. The city shall have a lien upon each such vehicle for the amount of the cost of removing and impounding such vehicle, plus such reasonable amount as may be charged by the depository for storing such vehicle. In the event such vehicle is stored at police headquarters the storage charge shall be one dollar ($1.00) per day. All such charges are hereby declared to be reasonable and proper charges to cover the cost of hauling to the depository or police headquarters and storage therein. No vehicle impounded as provided herein shall be released to any claimant without the payment of the charges provided in this section. The payment of any charges prescribed by this section shall not have the effect of relieving the owner, operator or claimant of the vehicle from any penalty prescribed by any other ordinance of the city or from trial and conviction for the violation of any other ordinance of the city. 
(Ord. No. V-1A, § 4, 6-6-67) 
Sec. 23-125. - Auction of unclaimed vehicles. 
    At least once each six (6) months, the chief of police shall sell at public auction to the highest bidder for cash each such vehicle impounded as provided herein which has been stored for a period of three (3) months or more, such sales to be made after notice of the time and place thereof shall have first been given by publication of notice once a week for two (2) successive weeks in a newspaper of general circulation published in the city, the first publication shall be at least twenty (20) days prior to such sale. After such publication the owner of any such vehicle so advertised may redeem the same at any time prior to its sale by paying the reasonable expenses and charges as set forth herein and a prorate of the cost of such publication. The chief of police of the city shall sell each vehicle separately and shall make a notation in the permanent storage record book of the amount received for each vehicle. The chief of police of the city shall have the right to reject any and all bids if the amount bid be unreasonably low and shall have the right to continue the sales from time to time if no bidders are present. After deducting and paying all expenses incurred in the taking up, storing, maintaining and selling of the vehicle, the balance, if any, shall be paid to the city clerk and shall be deposited by the city clerk to the general fund of the city. 
(Ord. No. V-1A, § 5, 6-6-67) 
Secs. 23-126-23-140. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE VII. - VEHICLES FOR HIRE[4] 
Footnotes: 
--- (4) --- 
Editor's note- Ordinance No. 16-80-97, adopted June 10, 1997, did not specifically amend the Code; hence, codification of the substantive provisions as §§ 23-141, 23-161-23-169 was at the discretion of the editor. 

DIVISION 1. - GENERALLY 

Sec. 23-141. - Subjection to traffic laws. 
    All motor vehicles engaged in the business of transporting passengers for hire within the city shall be subject to the traffic laws of the city. 
(Ord. No. 16-80-97, 6-10-97) 
Secs. 23-142-23-160. - Reserved. 
DIVISION 2. - AMBULANCES 

Sec. 23-161. - Definitions. 
    For the purpose of this article, the following terms shall have the meanings respectively ascribed to them: 
    Ambulance means a motor vehicle licensed by the state board of health and specially designed for, equipped or used as an emergency vehicle for the purpose of transporting persons who are wounded, injured, ill or sick, and shall include, but is not restricted to, emergency vehicles used for such purposes. 
    Ambulance attendant means any individual who is duly licensed by the state board of health as an emergency medical technician, advanced. 
    Ambulance driver means any individual who is duly licensed by the state board of health as an emergency medical technician and as an ambulance driver and has successfully completed a defensive driving course. 
    Ambulance service operator means any person engaged in the business of dispatching and operating an ambulance, who is duly licensed by the state board of health as an ambulance service operator. 
    Patient means an individual who is wounded, injured, ill or sick, or otherwise incapacitated or helpless. 
    State board of health means that body created by section 22-2-1 et seq., Code of Alabama, 1975, as amended, otherwise known as the Alabama State Board of Health of the Alabama Department of Public Health. 
(Ord. No. 16-80-97, 6-10-97) 
Sec. 23-162. - Applicability of article-Patient transport. 
    The provisions of this article shall not apply to the operation of any ambulance while traveling without a patient into, through or from the city; while being used to transport a patient through the city without stopping in the city; or while being used to transport a patient from outside the city to a location within the city. 
(Ord. No. 16-80-97, 6-10-97) 
Sec. 23-163. - Same-Prior ambulance operators. 
    Each person seeking to operate ambulances upon the streets of the city shall comply fully with the provisions hereof. 
(Ord. No. 16-80-97, 6-10-97) 
Sec. 23-164. - Same-Rescue squads. 
    The provisions of this article shall also apply to any rescue squad operating within the city; provided there shall not be required of the rescue squad, or volunteer members thereof while working for the rescue squad, any fee for licenses or permits issued hereunder. 
(Ord. No. 16-80-97, 6-10-97) 
Sec. 23-165. - Permits required. 
(a)  No person, either as owner, agent or otherwise, shall furnish, operate, conduct, maintain or otherwise be engaged in or profess to be engaged in the business or service of the transportation of patients upon the streets, public ways or other places in the city, unless such person holds a currently valid permit issued pursuant to this article. 
(b)  No ambulance shall be operated for ambulance purposes, and no individual shall drive, attend or permit to be operated a vehicle for such purposes on the streets, public ways or other places of the city, unless such ambulance shall be under the immediate supervision and direction of an individual who holds a currently valid permit as an ambulance attendant, and no such ambulance shall be operated for such purposes unless the attendant is accompanied at all times by an ambulance driver who holds a currently valid permit as a driver. 
(c)  No permit shall be required for an ambulance operator, attendant or driver of an ambulance which is rendering assistance to ambulances for which permits have been issued in case of a major catastrophe or emergency with which the ambulances of the city for which permits have been issued are insufficient or unable to cope. 
(d)  Except as otherwise provided in this article, it shall be unlawful for any person to engage in the business of operating an ambulance upon, over or along any street in the city, unless such person holds a valid, unrevoked and unsuspended permit therefor from the city council, granted by resolution. 
(e)  The requirements for a permit under this article shall be in addition to the requirements of a business privilege license. No business license shall be issued to any person to operate an ambulance in the city unless such person holds a currently valid, unrevoked and unsuspended ambulance service operator permit issued pursuant to this article. 
(f)  Each operator permit holder shall furnish a full and complete list of all personnel employed by such permit holder at any time requested by the chief of police. 
(Ord. No. 16-80-97, 6-10-97) 
Sec. 23-166. - Operator permit-Application. 
    Application for an ambulance operator permit issued hereunder shall be verified by oath of the applicant and shall be submitted to the city council by application filed with the city clerk along with a license fee of twenty-five dollars ($25.00) per ambulance. The application shall supply the following information: 
(1)  Name and home address of the applicant. 
(2)  Name and home address of the owner of the ambulance business. 
(3)  The location and description of the place or places from which the business intends to operate. 
(4)  The trade name, corporate name and other business name or designation, if any, under which the applicant does business and proposes to do business. 
(5)  The training and experience of the applicant and any employees of the applicant in the transportation and care of patients. 
(6)  A description of each ambulance, including make, model, year of manufacture, motor and chassis number, current state license number, length of time the ambulance has been in use, current odometer reading on the ambulance, and the color scheme, insignia, name, monogram or other distinguishing characteristics to be used to designate the applicant's ambulance. 
(7)  The location and description of the ambulances owned or operated by the applicant. 
(8)  State driver's license number for each attendant and driver, the date first licensed, the date and duration of any period when the license was suspended or revoked or canceled, and the expiration date of the current license. 
(9)  State license number for ambulance service operators and for each attendant and driver, the date first licensed, and the expiration date of the current license. 
(10)  Such other information as the city council shall find reasonably necessary to effectuate the purpose of this article and to arrive at a fair determination of whether the terms of this article have been complied with. 
(Ord. No. 16-80-97, 6-10-97) 
Sec. 23-167. - Same-Investigation of applicant. 
(a)  Each application for an ambulance operator permit filed with the city clerk shall be immediately referred to the chief of police for investigation and report. The chief shall investigate the facts set out in the application and report in writing to the city council within twenty-one (21) days the results of such chief's investigation as follows: 
(1)  The chief's finding of the truth or falsity of the facts set out in the application. 
(2)  Whether or not each ambulance, its required equipment, and the premises designated in the application meet the requirements of this article and other applicable laws, ordinances and regulations. 
(3)  Whether or not only duly licensed attendants and drivers are employed or are to be employed in such capacities. 
(4)  Any facts which the chief has which may bear upon the question of whether or not the applicant is a responsible and proper person to conduct, carry on, or engage in the proposed business. 
(5)  Whether or not the requirements of this article and all other applicable laws, ordinances, and regulations relating to the application have been met. 
(b)  A copy of the report of the chief shall be sent by the city clerk by certified mail to the applicant at the address listed on the application, on the same day which the report is submitted to the city council. 
(Ord. No. 16-80-97, 6-10-97) 
Sec. 23-168. - Same-Hearing on application. 
    Upon receipt of the report of the chief of police, the city council shall set a date for a hearing on the application to be held within fourteen (14) days after the receipt of such report. The city clerk shall notify the applicant, by certified mail, of the time and place of such hearing. The city clerk shall also cause notice of such hearing to be published once in a newspaper of general circulation in the city at least five (5) days prior to the date of the hearing. The applicant may appear before the city council and present evidence as to why the permit should be issued. Any other interested person may appear before the council and present evidence as to why the permit should be either issued or denied. At the hearing, the city council shall hear all evidence offered by any person that is relevant to the application and the inquiry required to determine whether the applicant meets the standards for issuance of a permit. 
(Ord. No. 16-80-97, 6-10-97) 
Sec. 23-169. - Same-Issuance; consideration by city council. 
(a)  The city council shall authorize and direct the chief of police to issue an operator's permit to the applicant if the city council finds that: 
(1)  The public convenience and necessity require the proposed ambulance service for which the application has been submitted. 
(2)  Insurance policies as required by this article have been approved and filed with the city clerk. 
(3)  The applicant and all attendants and drivers are fit and proper persons to conduct or work in the proposed business. 
(4)  All ambulances of the applicant are in good mechanical condition; are suitable for the transportation of patients from the standpoint of health, sanitation and safety; are maintained in suitable premises; and currently comply with all applicable laws and ordinances relating to health, sanitation and safety. 
(5)  At least one (1) ambulance of the applicant will be available to receive and immediately respond to all calls on a twenty-four-hour-per-day basis. 
(6)  The drivers and attendants employed by the applicant have current permits pursuant to this article. 
(7)  All ambulances are equipped with two-way radio equipment, lights, sirens and other equipment prescribed in this article. 
(8)  The requirements of this article and all other governing laws and ordinances have been met. 
(b)  In determining whether public convenience and necessity require the licensing of the proposed ambulance service, the city council shall consider whether the public is adequately served by other ambulance services, the financial responsibility of the applicant, the number, the kind and type of equipment, and the increased congestion upon the streets of the city. 
(Ord. No. 16-80-97, 6-10-97) 
Secs. 23-170-23-190. - Reserved. 
DIVISION 3. - ROTATION WRECKER AND TOWING SERVICE[5] 

Footnotes: 
--- (5) --- 
Editor's note- Ord. No. 2006-08-22(1), §§ 1-13, adopted August 22, 2006, amended div. 3 in its entirety to read as herein set out. Former div. 3, §§ 23-191-23-203, pertained to similar subject matter, and derived from Ord. No. 13-32-W-98, §§ 1-13. 

Sec. 23-191. - Definitions. 
    For the purpose of this division, the following terms, phrases, words and their derivations shall have the meaning given herein. When not inconsistent with the context, words used in the present tense include the future, words used in the singular number include the plural, and words in the male gender shall include the female and neuter. The work [word] "shall" is always mandatory and not merely directory. 
    Chief of police is the Chief of the Police Department of the City of Oneonta and may act through his designee for the purposes of this division. 
    City is the City of Oneonta, Alabama, and police jurisdiction. 
    Council is the governing body of the City of Oneonta. 
    Person is any person, firm, partnership, association, corporation, company or organization of any kind. 
    Street is any public road, street, avenue, highway or alley, within the city limits and police jurisdiction of Oneonta, Alabama. 
    Vehicle is any device in, upon or by which any person or property is or may be transported upon a street. 
    Wrecker is a person engaged in the business, or offering the services, of a vehicle wrecker or towing service, whereby disabled vehicles are towed or otherwise removed from the place where they are disabled by use of a truck, automobile or other vehicle so adapted to or designed for that purpose. 
(Ord. No. 2006-08-22(1), § 1, 8-22-2006) 
Sec. 23-192. - License required. 
    No wrecker shall engage in business or offer such service within the city without first obtaining a license to do business from the city as provided in this division. 
(Ord. No. 2006-08-22(1), § 2, 8-22-2006) 
Sec. 23-193. - Application for rotation wrecker service. 
    Applications for rotation wrecker service issued hereunder shall be made upon blank forms prepared and made available by the chief of police and shall state: 
(a)  The name and kind of legal entity, trade name (if any), home address, proposed business address, and business phone number(s) of the person making application. 
(b)  The location, description and hourly availability or the tow trucks owned or operated by the applicant. 
(c)  That the applicant has available space for properly accommodating and protecting all disabled vehicles to be towed or otherwise removed from the place where they are disabled. 
(d)  An agreement that the name of the wrecker is and will be kept prominently displayed on each tow truck. 
(e)  The description, size and location of a fenced-in area maintained by applicant under lock and key, to protect the vehicles towed in and contents thereof, by the wrecker. 
(f)  An agreement that the applicant will obey and comply with the terms and provisions of this ordinance and all laws relating to the towing or storage of vehicles for the public, and that applicant will to the best of his ability cause his employees to obey and comply with the terms and provisions of this ordinance and all laws relating to the towing or storage of vehicles for the public. 
(g)  An agreement that applicant remove any glass or other injurious material and otherwise clean up the scene of the wreck or collision before removing a vehicle from the scene. 
(h)  Such other information as the chief of police shall find reasonably necessary to effectuate the purpose of this ordinance and to arrive at a fair determination of whether the terms of this division have been complied with. 
(Ord. No. 2006-08-22(1), § 3, 8-22-2006) 
Sec. 23-194. - Insurance policies required. 
    No rotation wrecker status shall be issued to an applicant until he deposits with the chief of police a certificate or other assurance of insurance policies as follows: 
(a)  Garage keeper's policy. A garage keeper's legal liability policy covering fire, theft, and explosion in the minimum amounts of fifty thousand dollars ($50,000.00) and collision coverage subject to one hundred dollars ($100.00) deductible, with each accident deemed a separate claim. 
(b)  Garage liability policy. A garage liability policy covering the operation of applicant's business, equipment of vehicles, for any bodily injury or property damage. This policy will be in the minimum amounts of seven hundred fifty thousand dollars ($750,000.00) for any one (1) person killed or injured, and fifty thousand dollars ($50,000.00) for all damage arising out of injury to or destruction of property. 
(c)  [Notice.] Each policy required herein shall not be cancelled, terminated, or have any material changes made, before the rotation wrecker service has given thirty (30) days' notice to the chief of police. 
(Ord. No. 2006-08-22(1), § 4, 8-22-2006) 
Sec. 23-195. - Investigation. 
    Within seven (7) days after receipt of an application, the chief of police shall cause a background investigation of the applicant and an inspection of the proper vehicle licenses to each wrecker covered under this division. 
(Ord. No. 2006-08-22(1), § 5, 8-22-2006) 
Sec. 23-196. - Standards for insurance. 
    The police department shall issue rotation status when their investigation and inspection reveals: 
(a)  That the public conveyance and necessity require the proposed wrecker service for which application has been submitted; 
(b)  That insurance policies as required by this ordinance have been procured; 
(c)  That the applicant and all employees are fit and proper persons to conduct or work in the proposed business. 
(d)  A vehicle/wrecker mechanical and equipment inspection that will be performed by the police department, that all mechanical and safety equipment is properly attached and/or supplied with each wrecker inspected. 
(e)  That the requirements of this ordinance and all other governing laws and ordinances have been met. 
(Ord. No. 2006-08-22(1), § 6, 8-22-2006) 
Sec. 23-197. - Promulgation of regulations. 
    The chief of police is authorized to promulgate and enforce reasonable rules and regulations for wreckers pertaining to this ordinance and applicable local, state and federal laws. 
(Ord. No. 2006-08-22(1), § 7, 8-22-2006) 
Sec. 23-198. - Duties of rotation wrecker services. 
    A rotation wrecker status shall be issued subject to the following conditions which are the obligation of the wrecker services. 
(a)  Maintenance of equipment. Wreckers shall keep and maintain towing equipment which is adequate to perform such towing service in a reasonably workman like manner. 
(b)  Interception of emergency calls. No wrecker shall intercept police or fire calls by monitoring a scanner or other device to "jump" calls or go when not requested. 
(c)  Rotation of city towing. Wreckers shall perform towing service for the city on a rotation basis if they meet the requirements of this division. 
(Ord. No. 2006-08-22(1), § 8, 8-22-2006) 
Sec. 23-199. - General operation. 
(a)  No rotation wrecker shall proceed to the scene of a collision or accident without being requested to do so by the police department or the owner or person in charge of the vehicle. No rotation wrecker shall solicit business at the scene of a collision or accident. 
(b)  Each vehicle designed for or adapted for the purpose of a vehicle wrecker or towing service business shall be equipped with a flashing amber caution light properly installed. Said caution light shall be operated at the scene of a wreck or collision and while a disabled vehicle is being towed, but shall not be operated while proceeding to the scene of a wreck or collision, unless the dispatcher in the police department authorized use of said light in a particular case because of an emergency situation. 
(Ord. No. 2006-08-22(1), § 9, 8-22-2006) 
Sec. 23-200. - Standard equipment. 
    Each rotation wrecker shall maintain the following standard equipment on every tow truck: 
(a)  Power winch, winch line and boom with lifting capacity of eight thousand (8,000) pounds, factory rated, dual line capacity. 
(b)  One "sling" and "stay bar" or other similar device capable of protecting a vehicle being towed. 
(c)  Safety chains. 
(d)  Fire extinguisher. 
(e)  One four foot pry bar or wrecker bar capable of prying open doors. 
(f)  One broom. 
(g)  One shovel. 
(h)  One set of road flares. 
(i)  Emergency flasher system capable of emitting two amber lights to the front and two red lights to the rear of the vehicle and which shall flash simultaneously. 
(j)  One dolly, with name of wrecker permanently affixed. 
(Ord. No. 2006-08-22(1), § 10, 8-22-2006) 
Sec. 23-201. - Operation of rotation system. 
(a)  Wreckers granted rotation status may participate in the rotation system if they meet the following additional requirements. 
(1)  The applicant has and maintains in good condition at least two (2) three- quarter-ton capacity vehicle designed for or adapted to the purpose of a vehicle wrecker or towing service business.. 
(2)  The applicant maintains a storage lot within the police jurisdiction of Oneonta in an area that can accommodate a minimum of ten (10) vehicles, with no less than two thousand (2,000) square feet of storage lot space, enclosed by an appropriately designed fence consistent with state law, at least six (6) feet high, under lock and key, to protect the disabled vehicle and the contents thereof towed in by the wrecker. 
(3)  During the entire time a wrecker is on the rotation list, the wrecker shall be capable of furnishing ample equipment to service an accident involving one (1) vehicle. 
(4)  Maintain twenty-four-hour, seven-day a week service. Any operator who develops a pattern of failing to respond when requested may be removed from the rotation list. 
(5)  Applicant's primary place of business is located within the police jurisdiction of Oneonta. 
(6)  Wreckers or towing services must have all wreckers with wheel lift capabilities. 
(7)  Two-way communication equipment between the tow truck and wrecker's dispatcher. 
(8)  Wrecker services may use a flatbed, roll-back, or slide-back carrier to answer a rotation call when necessary or feasible. 
(9)  Authorization for rotation shall be considered personal to the holder thereof, and shall be issued only to some definite legal business operating a wrecker service, and shall not be subject to lease, nor shall the holder thereof sublet or permit the exercise by another in any manner, of the rights or privileges granted thereunder. Authorization for rotations is void if the business address or location of the facilities are changed, outside the police jurisdiction of the City of Oneonta. 
(10)  Each wrecker business will furnish the Oneonta Police Department with one (1) telephone number to be used for request for service during the day and one (1) number for night and weekends or a 24-hour telephone number. Answering services will be allowed at the discretion of the police chief. No pagers are permitted as a lone contact number. 
(11)  No wrecker operator shall respond to a call when he has consumed alcohol in any amount or has ingested either prescription or non-prescription drugs that may impair motor skills. 
(12)  No owner or operator shall be on the rotation list who has been convicted of grand larceny, theft of property, or similar felony, or misdemeanor offenses, involving force, violence or moral turpitude. 
(13)  No owner or operator shall be on the rotation list unless the said driver or owner is proficient and competent in operation of said wrecker. 
(14)  No person shall operate or be allowed to operate any wrecker for hire unless such operator has a valid Alabama drivers license or commercial driver's license, and applicable bond on the vehicle being used for towing purposes. 
(15)  At no time will a tow truck attach to a vehicle, which, by its size and/or weight would make towing said vehicle an unsafe movement. 
(16)  Wrecker services on rotation will collect a ten-dollar ($10.00) administration fee for the City of Oneonta on each rotation tow made in the City of Oneonta, to be paid by the rotation wrecker service on a monthly basis. 
(17)  The wrecker service is required to respond with its own wreckers and shall not send another wrecker service in response to a service call. The wrecker operator may be assisted by another wrecker service. 
(18)  The base rate of towing and storage will be set by the mayor and city council as recommended from time to time by the chief of police, in agreement with the rotation wrecker services involved. Any wrecker service requesting to be placed on rotation must agree to comply substantially with such base rates. Any request to change the base rate for towing and storage will be made in writing to the chief of police. 
The current rate for towing is not more than one hundred twenty-five ($125.00) and the current rate for storage is not more than thirty-five dollars ($35.00) per day. The rate for towing does not include the twenty-five dollars ($25.00) administrative fee referred to in item (16) above. The rate for storage shall begin to be assessed at the time the towed vehicle arrives on the storage lot. 
No other fees may be assessed on any normal rotation calls for the City of Oneonta, including accidents. However, any special circumstances may incur additional expenses. 
(19)  Any wrecker service on rotation must be open between the hours of 8:00 a.m. until 4:00 p.m., Monday through Friday, and have someone available on Saturday and Sunday at a reasonable time for the purpose of releasing vehicles towed by the Oneonta Police Department. Any vehicle towed by the Oneonta Police Department based on arrest or traffic violation must not be released until a written release is first obtained by the owner or designated agent of owner, from the Oneonta Police Department. 
(b)  Wreckers meeting the requirements of subsection (a) shall be placed on a rotation list to be maintained by the chief of police. A request to the police department for a wrecker, when the operator or owner does not request a particular wrecker, shall be filled according to the rotation schedule by the next wrecker on the schedule. It shall be the duty of the wrecker who is scheduled to respond when called to provide the service requested. If a wrecker cannot provide the service requested within twenty (20) minutes, the next wrecker on the rotation list shall be called. No wrecker shall accept a request for service unless a tow truck is immediately available to perform the requested service. Repeated tardiness will result in a suspension from the rotation list. 
(Ord. No. 2006-08-22(1), § 11, 8-22-2006; Ord. No. 2015-5-12A-WR , 5-12-15; Ord. of 12-12-2017(1), § 1 ) 
Sec. 23-202. - Applications for rotation list designation. 
(a)  Each wrecker desiring to be placed on the rotation list shall file a written request to the police chief. 
(b)  The police chief will furnish each wrecker a copy of the rules and regulations pertaining to the operation of wreckers on the rotation list. 
(c)  The police chief will conduct an investigation of the requesting wrecker business and determine if the business meets all qualifications to be placed on the rotation list. 
(d)  The police chief has the right to inspect any tow truck operated by a wrecker on the rotation list at any time to insure it is maintained for safety and all equipment that is required is on the tow truck and in proper operating order. 
(e)  Police officers will not make recommendations as to a particular wrecker service, but ask the vehicles' operator if they have a preference as to which wrecker to send or notify communications to go by rotation. 
(Ord. No. 2006-08-22(1), § 12, 8-22-2006) 
Sec. 23-203. - Penalty for violation of this division. 
    Any rotation wrecker service that violates this division, or any part or section of this division may be suspended or removed from rotation status.
